<h2 class='date-header'><span>Sunday, February 07, 2010</span></h2>

        <div class="date-posts">
      
<div class='post-outer'>
<div class='post'>
<a name='7383991930503755065'></a>
<h3 class='post-title'>
<a href='http://www.hawkowlsnest.com/2010/02/puerto-rico-day-6-last-day-and-final.html'>Puerto Rico Day 6: Last day and final thoughts</a>
</h3>
<div class='post-header-line-1'></div>
<div class='post-body'>
<p><p>We spent the night at <a href="http://www.casacubuy.com/">Casa Cubuy</a> eco-lodge. It&#8217;s a really nice spot overlooking the rainforest. There&#8217;s a river and waterfalls nearby. It&#8217;s very open, but covered from the rain. There are lots of comfy seats, a little fridge with beer and wine for purchase, and lots of hammocks. It could benefit from some bird feeders. The rooms are nicely decorated, although ours had quirky 4-poster beds which didn&#8217;t really match the eco-lodge theme. The rooms were clean and comfortable. Like many tropical sites, they had the &#8220;no flushing toilet paper&#8221; rule. </p><p><a href="http://lh3.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S25LOG2oubI/AAAAAAAABJs/zGhVCy-pnPk/s1600-h/IMG_4562%5B2%5D.jpg"><img title="IMG_4562" style="BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; BORDER-TOP: 0px; DISPLAY: block; FLOAT: none; MARGIN-LEFT: auto; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; MARGIN-RIGHT: auto; BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px" height="310" alt="IMG_4562" src="http://lh6.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S25LOeJezhI/AAAAAAAABJw/KLra0vA6czg/IMG_4562_thumb.jpg?imgmax=800" width="412" border="0" /></a> </p><p>It rained all night and into the morning. We spent 45 minutes or so on the deck, but didn&#8217;t see many birds. It was pretty foggy. We did have great views of Greater Antillean Oriole. I&#8217;ve heard the breakfasts at Casa Cubuy are great, but we didn&#8217;t stay.</p><p><a href="http://lh3.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S25LOjAeUiI/AAAAAAAABJ0/QVmlJBMJzo8/s1600-h/IMG_4588%5B2%5D.jpg"><img title="IMG_4588" style="BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; BORDER-TOP: 0px; DISPLAY: block; FLOAT: none; MARGIN-LEFT: auto; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; MARGIN-RIGHT: auto; BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px" height="310" alt="IMG_4588" src="http://lh6.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S25LO8eUIxI/AAAAAAAABJ4/WenbRV1uuN0/IMG_4588_thumb.jpg?imgmax=800" width="412" border="0" /></a> </p><p>We packed up for our journey toward the airport. We stopped for breakfast at the <a href="http://www.fajardoinn.com/">Fajardo Inn</a>. Not only is this a nice resort with good breakfast, the grounds are a great place to see two sought-after hummingbirds: Green-throated Carib and Antillean Crested Hummingbird. We were not disappointed. Both hummingbirds were right there in the parking lot! We also saw Nutmeg Mannikins and another Greater Antillean Oriole.</p><p><a href="http://lh4.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S25LPMpxggI/AAAAAAAABJ8/1UHoG0MSijw/s1600-h/carib%5B2%5D.jpg"><img title="carib" style="BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; BORDER-TOP: 0px; DISPLAY: inline; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px" height="412" alt="carib" src="http://lh4.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S25LPfYE85I/AAAAAAAABKA/6IciXUitNC4/carib_thumb.jpg?imgmax=800" width="275" border="0" /></a> <br /><em>Green-throated Carib</em></p><p><a href="http://lh6.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S25LPneJROI/AAAAAAAABKE/B073nQvknYI/s1600-h/crested%20hummer%5B2%5D.jpg"><em><img title="crested hummer" style="BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; BORDER-TOP: 0px; DISPLAY: block; FLOAT: none; MARGIN-LEFT: auto; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; MARGIN-RIGHT: auto; BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px" height="276" alt="crested hummer" src="http://lh4.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S25LP7xO1ZI/AAAAAAAABKI/vi2PcjKLz14/crested%20hummer_thumb.jpg?imgmax=800" width="412" border="0" /></em></a><em>Antillean Crested Hummingbird </em></p><p><a href="http://lh3.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S25LQQ0TNhI/AAAAAAAABKM/K6EpvdrlEIM/s1600-h/oriole%5B2%5D.jpg"><em><img title="oriole" style="BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; BORDER-TOP: 0px; DISPLAY: inline; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px" height="276" alt="oriole" src="http://lh3.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S25LQQRvA0I/AAAAAAAABKQ/KUXWrmLv1Do/oriole_thumb.jpg?imgmax=800" width="412" border="0" /></em></a><em> <br />Greater Antillean Oriole<br /></em></p><p>We made a few stops in El Yunque in hopes of seeing Puerto Rican Parrots, but we didn&#8217;t find any. We did see some nice waterfalls and a Black-throated Blue Warbler. </p><p><a href="http://lh5.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S25LQ_H7o1I/AAAAAAAABKU/Ys0-weurO1U/s1600-h/IMG_4594%5B2%5D.jpg"><img title="IMG_4594" style="BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; BORDER-TOP: 0px; DISPLAY: block; FLOAT: none; MARGIN-LEFT: auto; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; MARGIN-RIGHT: auto; BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px" height="412" alt="IMG_4594" src="http://lh4.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S25LRJJRw9I/AAAAAAAABKY/klBMmHcxj1I/IMG_4594_thumb.jpg?imgmax=800" width="310" border="0" /></a> </p><p>Thus ended our trip in Puerto Rico. I had a blast. I highly recommend Wildside Nature Tours. My experience was great with very competent, flexible, and personable leaders. Others who have done trips with them have said similar things. Thanks again to <a href="http://www.10000birds.com/">10,000 Birds</a> and <a href="http://www.wildsidetoursinc.com/">Wildside Nature Tours</a> for sponsoring the contest that got me there! </p><p><a href="http://www.hawkowlsnest.com/2010/02/puerto-rico-day-6-last-day-and-final.html">Go to Day 6</a></p></p>
<div style='clear: both;'></div>

<h2 class='date-header'><span>Saturday, February 06, 2010</span></h2>

        <div class="date-posts">
      
<div class='post-outer'>
<div class='post'>
<a name='6474088707962158895'></a>
<h3 class='post-title'>
<a href='http://www.hawkowlsnest.com/2010/02/puerto-rico-day-5-finding-what-we.html'>Puerto Rico Day 5: Finding What We Missed</a>
</h3>
<div class='post-header-line-1'></div>
<div class='post-body'>
<p><p>We started around 6:00AM and headed back to Guanica State Forest to try once more for the <a href="http://audubon2.org/watchlist/viewSpecies.jsp?id=167">Puerto Rican Nightjar</a>. We drove to the forest, headed up the road at a closed gate, and stood waiting in the darkness. Actually, it was a bright moon, so it wasn&#8217;t really that dark. In any event, it wasn&#8217;t long before we heard a &#8220;Whirr!&#8221; of a nightjar. It was quite close, but deep enough in the dense woods that we couldn&#8217;t see it. We heard 1 or 2 others, but never did see one. It was cool knowing that we were hearing a bird that only exists in this small area of Puerto Rico and nowhere else on the planet. We also heard a Puerto Rican Screech Owl.</p><p>With one target species down, we grabbed breakfast and then hit the road. This was mostly a travel day to <a href="http://www.fs.fed.us/r8/caribbean/">El Yunque</a>, basically across the southern part of PR from west to east, but we did have a few more birding stops to pick up some other birds we hadn&#8217;t seen yet. Our first stop was back to the feeder area where we had less-than-desirable views of the Yellow-shouldered Blackbird the day before. This time there were several of them on trees near the feeding station. They were joined by some Shiny Cowbirds, a known nuisance to the blackbird&#8217;s population, and also a ton of Eurasian Collared-Doves. </p><p align="center"> <a href="http://lh5.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S22QVV4qA-I/AAAAAAAABIk/pYmYjeg3Z38/s1600-h/blackbird%5B5%5D.jpg"><img title="blackbird" style="BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; BORDER-TOP: 0px; DISPLAY: inline; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px" height="276" alt="blackbird" src="http://lh6.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S22QWDfwGbI/AAAAAAAABIo/CRsSageyJx8/blackbird_thumb%5B1%5D.jpg?imgmax=800" width="412" border="0" /></a><br /><em>Yellow-shouldered Blackbird</em></p><p>We then went back to Guanica State Forest for some daytime birding. It was quite windy and the forest was very quiet. We were standing around and listening when I saw something move in my peripheral vision. It was a Mangrove Cuckoo! </p><p align="center"><a href="http://lh4.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S22QWqj0TrI/AAAAAAAABIs/1RUhCEIdUPc/s1600-h/cuckoo%5B5%5D.jpg"><img title="cuckoo" style="BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; BORDER-TOP: 0px; DISPLAY: block; FLOAT: none; MARGIN-LEFT: auto; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; MARGIN-RIGHT: auto; BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px" height="276" alt="cuckoo" src="http://lh5.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S22QW_WMr8I/AAAAAAAABIw/mTQXw14XZaA/cuckoo_thumb%5B1%5D.jpg?imgmax=800" width="412" border="0" /></a><em> Hello there!</em></p><p>We also had great looks at two Puerto Rican Todies. It&#8217;s hard to pick a favorite PR bird, but this one is certainly high on the list. Tody pictures below.</p><p align="center"><a href="http://lh3.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S22QXU0oAuI/AAAAAAAABI0/pcn75FvmwKY/s1600-h/tody01%5B2%5D.jpg"><img title="tody01" style="BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; BORDER-TOP: 0px; DISPLAY: block; FLOAT: none; MARGIN-LEFT: auto; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; MARGIN-RIGHT: auto; BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px" height="412" alt="tody01" src="http://lh3.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S22QXg6PZzI/AAAAAAAABI4/Jl4ETRIss2c/tody01_thumb.jpg?imgmax=800" width="277" border="0" /></a></p><p></p><p align="center"><a href="http://lh5.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S22QYLYXM5I/AAAAAAAABI8/jSlv7Zlt40U/s1600-h/tody02%5B2%5D.jpg"><img title="tody02" style="BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; BORDER-TOP: 0px; DISPLAY: block; FLOAT: none; MARGIN-LEFT: auto; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; MARGIN-RIGHT: auto; BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px" height="275" alt="tody02" src="http://lh4.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S22QYkfw7LI/AAAAAAAABJA/HyStFpoH5t4/tody02_thumb.jpg?imgmax=800" width="412" border="0" /></a></p><p></p><p>Our next stop was back to Laguna Cartajena NWR to look for West Indian Whistling-Ducks. While looking for them, we found a couple Least Grebes, a bird I hadn&#8217;t seen since 2005 in South Texas. I like their beady little eyes. We had terrific views of one West Indian Whistling-Duck flying by, but it landed out of view. The sky was filled with Cave Swallows and I was able to pick out an oddball in the group, which turned out to be a Caribbean Martin. We had a long ride ahead of us and one more birding spot.</p><p align="center"><a href="http://lh3.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S22QZCgdQ0I/AAAAAAAABJE/-OsTFc2QjxE/s1600-h/coot%5B2%5D.jpg"><img title="coot" style="BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; BORDER-TOP: 0px; DISPLAY: inline; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px" height="276" alt="coot" src="http://lh3.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S22QZhxn7DI/AAAAAAAABJI/ADPcUzXRO5Y/coot_thumb.jpg?imgmax=800" width="412" border="0" /></a><br /><em>Caribbean Coot &#8211; Notice how high the white face shield goes up its head.<br /></p></em><p align="center"><em><a href="http://lh3.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S22QZ_Y2LMI/AAAAAAAABJM/R6uQAW7eEYA/s1600-h/cattleegrets%5B5%5D.jpg"><img title="cattleegrets" style="BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; BORDER-TOP: 0px; DISPLAY: block; FLOAT: none; MARGIN-LEFT: auto; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; MARGIN-RIGHT: auto; BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px" height="276" alt="cattleegrets" src="http://lh5.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S22QaUfyieI/AAAAAAAABJQ/bR_N1qRszek/cattleegrets_thumb%5B1%5D.jpg?imgmax=800" width="412" border="0" /></a> Cattle Egrets are everywhere in PR</em> <br /></p><p>After a bit of a drive, a nap, and a stop at Sizzler (they still have those?), we stopped at a school baseball field in a tiny town. Oddly, this is the best spot in PR to see <a href="http://www.birdlife.org/datazone/species/index.html?action=SpcHTMDetails.asp&amp;sid=2487&amp;m=0">Plain Pigeon</a>* (what a name!), a rare Caribbean specialty. Sure enough, we quickly found one high in a tree on a hill side. It&#8217;s not as plain-looking as its name suggests. </p><p>After the pigeon site, we were on the road heading to El Yunque and the <a href="http://www.casacubuy.com/">Casa Cubuy</a> eco-lodge. We arrived at the lodge after dark. After dinner, we listened for screech owls. We heard one, but the wind and rain were not conducive to finding the bird. This was our last night in PR. Stay tuned for some cool hummingbirds and thoughts on Casa Cubuy in the next installment.</p><p></p><p></p><p></p><p></p><p></p><p></p><p></p><p></p><p>*I think the worst West Indian bird name goes to the <a href="http://www.mangoverde.com/wbg/spec/spec116-355.html">Sad Flycatcher</a>. </p></p>
<div style='clear: both;'></div>

<h2 class='date-header'><span>Friday, February 05, 2010</span></h2>

        <div class="date-posts">
      
<div class='post-outer'>
<div class='post'>
<a name='117892178050914033'></a>
<h3 class='post-title'>
<a href='http://www.hawkowlsnest.com/2010/02/puerto-rico-day-4-mountains-to-coast.html'>Puerto Rico Day 4: Mountains to the Coast</a>
</h3>
<div class='post-header-line-1'></div>
<div class='post-body'>
<p><p>We spent the night of day 3 at Hacienda Juanita, a lodge in the mountains on a banana and coffee plantation. It was a bit rustic, but comfortable enough. On the hotel grounds, we listened for the endemic <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Screech-owl">Puerto Rican Screech Owl</a> and heard multiple individuals. One was so close but it was straight up a rock wall that butted against the lodge. There was no way to see it.</p><p align="center"><a href="http://lh6.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2xvZfJcsUI/AAAAAAAABHU/L1jysBvjJ18/s1600-h/IMG_4474%5B2%5D.jpg"><img title="IMG_4474" style="BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; BORDER-TOP: 0px; DISPLAY: block; FLOAT: none; MARGIN-LEFT: auto; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; MARGIN-RIGHT: auto; BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px" height="310" alt="IMG_4474" src="http://lh4.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2xvaXOqMfI/AAAAAAAABHY/EdpU4LHu6aY/IMG_4474_thumb.jpg?imgmax=800" width="412" border="0" /></a></p><p><em>The view from the Hacienda Juanita</em> </p><p>We woke the morning of day 4 to find that our breakfast was slightly delayed. The cook wasn&#8217;t there yet, so we&#8217;d have to wait a little. We took the opportunity to do a little birding around the property and saw some of the same species we&#8217;d already seen. Breakfast was worth the wait. I had a great omelet and some hot harina cereal. Tasty! We also had good views of a female <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Emerald">Puerto Rican Emerald</a> (a hummingbird) from the breakfast table. After breakfast, I was buying coffee in the office when I heard one of the leaders call from outside, &#8220;<a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antillean_Euphonia">Antillean Euphonia</a>!&#8221; While not an endemic, it&#8217;s a much sought-after Caribbean species. We all had amazing looks at a male and female checking out bromeliads (that&#8217;s where they nest) in a large tree in the parking lot. What luck!</p><p align="center"><a href="http://lh3.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2xvbPE-0rI/AAAAAAAABHc/pVQNJgBLq9E/s1600-h/euphonia%5B2%5D.jpg"><img title="euphonia" style="BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; BORDER-TOP: 0px; DISPLAY: inline; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px" height="277" alt="euphonia" src="http://lh4.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2xvcKDHZhI/AAAAAAAABHg/Dic1s1NQR1o/euphonia_thumb.jpg?imgmax=800" width="412" border="0" /></a></p><p></p><p><em>Antillean Euphonia</em></p><p>We packed up and left Hacienda Juanita for another shot at the Lesser Antillean Pewee at the nearby fishery. Luck was with us again and it was there, flycatching from a perch over a creek. Neat bird! Too small and far for photos though. The late breakfast turned out to be a blessing in disguise.</p><p>We packed into the minivan again and made our way to the coast, specifically <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cabo_Rojo_National_Wildlife_Refuge">Cabo Rojo National Wildlife Refuge</a>. On our way there, the leader saw an odd animal cross the road. We did a u-turn to see what it was and it turned out to be&#8230; MONKEYS!  Macaques to be exact. There are no native monkeys on Puerto Rico. These are apparently escapes from a feral colony on a nearby island. No one knows how they got to the mainland, according to one local. </p><p align="center"><a href="http://lh6.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2xvdD9hb4I/AAAAAAAABHk/QGC00dtEMnI/s1600-h/monkeys%5B5%5D.jpg"><img title="monkeys" style="BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; BORDER-TOP: 0px; DISPLAY: block; FLOAT: none; MARGIN-LEFT: auto; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; MARGIN-RIGHT: auto; BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px" height="412" alt="monkeys" src="http://lh4.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2xveJqPFhI/AAAAAAAABHo/uI8zzgtjXRI/monkeys_thumb%5B1%5D.jpg?imgmax=800" width="275" border="0" /></a></p><p></p><p>Cabo Rojo is a GORGEOUS area in the southwest corner of PR with the turquoise waters of the Caribbean beating against red cliffs that give Cabo Rojo (the red coast) its name. It&#8217;s much drier than the rest of the places we had visited. We saw cacti and succulent plants all around.</p><p>We got our first taste of shorebirds for the trip at Cabo Rojo with side-by-side Greater and Lesser Yellowlegs, Ruddy Turnstone, Dunlin, and Spotted Sandpiper. A group of Royal Terns lounged atop a group of pilings as well. </p><p align="center"><a href="http://lh4.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2xvflQZuCI/AAAAAAAABHs/X7ZdKpE5ZEE/s1600-h/royal%20terns%5B2%5D.jpg"><img title="royal terns" style="BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; BORDER-TOP: 0px; DISPLAY: block; FLOAT: none; MARGIN-LEFT: auto; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; MARGIN-RIGHT: auto; BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px" height="276" alt="royal terns" src="http://lh4.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2xvgpA9q-I/AAAAAAAABHw/Pzq3j4xkvaM/royal%20terns_thumb.jpg?imgmax=800" width="412" border="0" /></a></p><p><em>Royal Terns</em></p><p> </p><p>The whole time, the <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Morrillos_Lighthouse">Los Morillos Lighthouse</a> loomed high on a cliff watching over us. </p><p align="center"><a href="http://lh5.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2xvhRzHyHI/AAAAAAAABH0/O8pqedZvzQM/s1600-h/IMG_4500%5B2%5D.jpg"><img title="IMG_4500" style="BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; BORDER-TOP: 0px; DISPLAY: block; FLOAT: none; MARGIN-LEFT: auto; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; MARGIN-RIGHT: auto; BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px" height="310" alt="IMG_4500" src="http://lh6.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2xvigUXmtI/AAAAAAAABH4/toRBNzjpf50/IMG_4500_thumb.jpg?imgmax=800" width="412" border="0" /></a></p><p></p><p>We walked up to the lighthouse to get a good view of the sea. The view was breathtaking.</p><p><a href="http://lh4.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2xvjS36vXI/AAAAAAAABH8/ED33ursoZCg/s1600-h/IMG_4531%5B2%5D.jpg"><img title="IMG_4531" style="BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; BORDER-TOP: 0px; DISPLAY: block; FLOAT: none; MARGIN-LEFT: auto; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; MARGIN-RIGHT: auto; BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px" height="310" alt="IMG_4531" src="http://lh6.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2xvkDAJ_3I/AAAAAAAABIA/NfxmjbTA2V4/IMG_4531_thumb.jpg?imgmax=800" width="412" border="0" /></a> </p><p>A Brown Booby soared right over our heads and joined a dozen of its brethren on a large rock in the sea. I had distant views of these birds in Australia, but these views were fantastic, although the light was harsh and my photos reflect that.</p><p><a href="http://lh3.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2xvkz1XhJI/AAAAAAAABIE/QwFpc3cfPY8/s1600-h/brownbooby%5B2%5D.jpg"><img title="brownbooby" style="BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; BORDER-TOP: 0px; DISPLAY: inline; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px" height="276" alt="brownbooby" src="http://lh4.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2xvlkyR9rI/AAAAAAAABII/C_zdBYmedtc/brownbooby_thumb.jpg?imgmax=800" width="412" border="0" /></a> </p><p><a href="http://lh6.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2xvmiMrqYI/AAAAAAAABIM/w8dbNo0atXg/s1600-h/brownbooby2%5B2%5D.jpg"><img title="brownbooby2" style="BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; BORDER-TOP: 0px; DISPLAY: inline; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px" height="277" alt="brownbooby2" src="http://lh3.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2xvnbjRRRI/AAAAAAAABIQ/3ew_eEMAs34/brownbooby2_thumb.jpg?imgmax=800" width="412" border="0" /></a> </p><p>We left Cabo Rojo and continued to <a href="http://www.fws.gov/Refuges/profiles/index.cfm?id=41527">Laguna Cartajena NWR</a>, a large marsh and home to Caribbean Coots and <a href="http://www.whistlingduck.org/">West Indian Whistling-Ducks</a>. This was one of my favorite stops on the trip. I love waterfowl and wading birds and this place was chock full of them. Caribbean Coots were plentiful along with Common Moorhens, a few Purple Gallinules, Ruddy Ducks, White-cheeked Pintails, and 9 species of waders. We even had a chance to compare American Coots to Caribbean Coots. The Caribbean&#8217;s fast shield extends further up the head than the American&#8217;s. We looked for the West Indian Whistling-Duck, but didn&#8217;t see one. So we planned to return the next day, since we had something big waiting for us.</p><p><a href="http://lh3.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2xvofHVVhI/AAAAAAAABIU/gqaWtaSIQv4/s1600-h/IMG_4542%5B2%5D.jpg"><img title="IMG_4542" style="BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; BORDER-TOP: 0px; DISPLAY: block; FLOAT: none; MARGIN-LEFT: auto; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; MARGIN-RIGHT: auto; BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px" height="310" alt="IMG_4542" src="http://lh5.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2xvpZmX9PI/AAAAAAAABIY/nyE8IueL6Rs/IMG_4542_thumb.jpg?imgmax=800" width="412" border="0" /></a> </p><p>We left Laguna Cartajena and headed to the town of Parguera, looking for the endangered and endemic <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yellow-shouldered_Blackbird">Yellow-shouldered Blackbird</a>. They live in the mangroves, but come to a local feeder next to a little store each afternoon. Our timing was a bit late and the birds were already in the mangroves. After much waiting, we did see a few birds silhouetted in a bare tree in the mangroves. These would have to wait for another try the next morning as well.</p><p>In the evening, we went to <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gu%C3%A1nica_State_Forest">Guanica State Forest</a>, the stronghold of the <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Nightjar">Puerto Rican Nightjar</a>. Unfortunately, we didn&#8217;t hear or see this rare species. It was incredibly windy and perhaps this kept the birds down. After much waiting, we decided to pack it in.</p><p><a href="http://lh4.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2xvqHADJwI/AAAAAAAABIc/RJxkWMLb3lU/s1600-h/IMG_4551%5B2%5D.jpg"><img title="IMG_4551" style="BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; BORDER-TOP: 0px; DISPLAY: block; FLOAT: none; MARGIN-LEFT: auto; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; MARGIN-RIGHT: auto; BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px" height="310" alt="IMG_4551" src="http://lh5.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2xvrHugF1I/AAAAAAAABIg/nuAhMjln-o4/IMG_4551_thumb.jpg?imgmax=800" width="412" border="0" /></a><em>My friend Mike shows the most comfy way to look for PR Nightjars </em></p><p>At dinner, we agreed to wake up extra early to try again for the nightjar. More on that in our next installment and more photos from Laguna Cartajena.</p><p><a href="http://www.hawkowlsnest.com/2010/02/puerto-rico-day-5-finding-what-we.html">Go to Day 5</a></p></p>

<h2 class='date-header'><span>Wednesday, February 03, 2010</span></h2>

        <div class="date-posts">
      
<div class='post-outer'>
<div class='post'>
<a name='642327587308739082'></a>
<h3 class='post-title'>
<a href='http://www.hawkowlsnest.com/2010/02/puerto-rico-day-3-rare-birds-and.html'>Puerto Rico Day 3: Rare Birds and Bacalao Ice Cream</a>
</h3>
<div class='post-header-line-1'></div>
<div class='post-body'>
<p><p align="center"><img title="IMG_4462" style="BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; BORDER-TOP: 0px; DISPLAY: block; FLOAT: none; MARGIN-LEFT: auto; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; MARGIN-RIGHT: auto; BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px" height="310" alt="IMG_4462" src="http://lh6.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2mMKVNnLLI/AAAAAAAABGg/iSarG9Ax5xI/IMG_4462_thumb.jpg?imgmax=800" width="412" border="0" /></p><p><em>Note: This is my first attempt to post with Windows Live Writer so I hope it doesn&#8217;t look like garbage.</em></p><p>We woke at an ungodly hour and had the equivalent of a NJ diner breakfast (not a bad thing) before departing for the Cambalache State Forest. This is a small, and I mean SMALL, plot of tropical forest that holds a surprising number of Puerto Rican endemics. Upon exiting the minivan, we immediately were hearing and seeing birds. </p><p>The first was the sing-song-y <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Vireo">Puerto Rican Vireo</a> which gave us great looks. He was followed by the cardinal-like call of the Puerto Rican Bullfinch which also gave stellar looks. The birds were coming quick. We heard the short bzzt of the <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Tody">Puerto Rican Tody</a>, but he remained out of sight. A loud call from around a bend was that of the <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Woodpecker">Puerto Rican Woodpecker</a> &#8211; a <em>Melanerpes</em> unlike any I had seen before. We had brief looks at one, but better looks were to come. A raucous rattle was that of the <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Lizard-Cuckoo">Puerto Rican Lizard-Cuckoo</a>, one of the birds I most wanted to see on the trip. It spent time high in a tree giving us views of just pieces of the bird at time. A nearby fart-like sound led us to crippling, eye-level views of the Puerto Rican Tody. As one person said, it looks like a lollipop and the bill is the stick. So true! It looks like it would taste good if you licked it. My photos of this one stink, but there were more to come later on the trip.</p><p align="center"><a href="http://lh6.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2mMKmEWPmI/AAAAAAAABGk/Hz03i4wTTms/s1600-h/Common%20Ground%20Dove%5B3%5D.jpg"><img title="Common Ground Dove" style="BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; BORDER-TOP: 0px; DISPLAY: inline; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px" height="276" alt="Common Ground Dove" src="http://lh4.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2mMLcjVl0I/AAAAAAAABGo/oIZOsUNOfkA/Common%20Ground%20Dove_thumb%5B1%5D.jpg?imgmax=800" width="412" border="0" /></a> </p><p align="center">A Common Ground-Dove</p><p> </p><p>We got crippling looks at the Puerto Rican Woodpecker in a hole in a telephone pole. This bird was too cool.</p><p align="center"><a href="http://lh3.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2mML5ceAHI/AAAAAAAABGs/wlDdnDMV5Cw/s1600-h/PRWoodpecker5.jpg"><img title="PR Woodpecker" style="BORDER-TOP-WIDTH: 0px; DISPLAY: inline; BORDER-LEFT-WIDTH: 0px; BORDER-BOTTOM-WIDTH: 0px; BORDER-RIGHT-WIDTH: 0px" height="276" alt="PR Woodpecker" src="http://lh6.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2mMMjnaJCI/AAAAAAAABGw/pnfDm0hqST4/PRWoodpecker_thumb3.jpg?imgmax=800" width="412" border="0" /></a><br /><em>Puerto Rican Woodpecker</em> </p><p align="center"><a href="http://lh4.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2mMNusIqlI/AAAAAAAABG0/vaJfsmGGCrI/s1600-h/PR%20Woodpecker2%5B2%5D.jpg"><img title="PR Woodpecker2" style="BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; BORDER-TOP: 0px; DISPLAY: inline; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px" height="310" alt="PR Woodpecker2" src="http://lh4.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2mMOE9CtgI/AAAAAAAABG4/OokhLWIC9zg/PR%20Woodpecker2_thumb.jpg?imgmax=800" width="412" border="0" /></a><br />Digiscoped shot</p><p>We then headed over to the Rio Abajo area in search of <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Parrot">Puerto Rican Parrots</a>. With less than 40 wild birds left, this came down to a matter of luck. Unfortunately, we didn&#8217;t see the birds, but did add Loggerhead Kingbird, Broad-winged Hawk (pretty rare in PR), and Scaly-naped Pigeon to our tally. We also saw the gorgeous flowers of the Poma Rosa or Rose Apple.</p><p><a href="http://lh3.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2mMOeokVkI/AAAAAAAABG8/Vj2KbNXDbv4/s1600-h/Rose%20Apple%5B2%5D.jpg"><img title="Rose Apple" style="BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; BORDER-TOP: 0px; DISPLAY: block; FLOAT: none; MARGIN-LEFT: auto; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; MARGIN-RIGHT: auto; BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px" height="276" alt="Rose Apple" src="http://lh5.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2mMPAW_DbI/AAAAAAAABHA/hFgdcRFz2m0/Rose%20Apple_thumb.jpg?imgmax=800" width="412" border="0" /></a> </p><p>On the road near Rio Abajo, we also spied Shiny Cowbird. An attractive blackbird, this bird has caused problems for the endemic <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yellow-shouldered_Blackbird">Yellow-shouldered Blackbird</a>.</p><p align="center"><a href="http://lh6.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2mMPTgfsoI/AAAAAAAABHE/Ip4IdeyY2Bw/s1600-h/Shiny%20Cowbird%5B2%5D.jpg"><img title="Shiny Cowbird" style="BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; BORDER-TOP: 0px; DISPLAY: inline; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px" height="277" alt="Shiny Cowbird" src="http://lh3.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2mMP-Se_2I/AAAAAAAABHI/NGv-0O6g9MM/Shiny%20Cowbird_thumb.jpg?imgmax=800" width="412" border="0" /></a><br />Shiny Cowbird</p><p>We stopped at a <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Helader%C3%ADa_de_Lares">famous ice cream shop</a> in the town of Lares. They are known for having hundreds of different flavors of ice cream including many non-traditional flavors like rum, ginger, garlic, rice &amp; beans, carrot, and the one I tried&#8230; SALT COD (AKA Bacalao). Even being a vegetarian, I couldn&#8217;t resist trying fish-flavored ice cream. You know how they say that things are an &#8220;acquired taste?&#8221; I don&#8217;t know how anyone could acquire a taste for it. Blech. I ended up getting one scoop of peanut and one scoop of sweet plantain. It was great.</p><p><a href="http://lh4.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2mMQ2HT6xI/AAAAAAAABHM/5fge7WFWI1E/s1600-h/IMG_4462%5B2%5D.jpg"><img title="IMG_4470" style="BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; BORDER-TOP: 0px; DISPLAY: block; FLOAT: none; MARGIN-LEFT: auto; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; MARGIN-RIGHT: auto; BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px" height="310" alt="IMG_4470" src="http://lh5.ggpht.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2mMRUrm9iI/AAAAAAAABHQ/sLvqQVJz-f4/IMG_4470%5B2%5D.jpg?imgmax=800" width="412" border="0" /> </a></p><p>We were back on the road again heading to <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maricao_State_Forest">Maricao State Forest</a>, home of the recently discovered (well, 1972) <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elfin-woods_Warbler">Elfin-woods Warbler</a>. It was late in the day. We paced up and down the road listening for its chip note (it doesn&#8217;t sing). After some time, we heard that chip and the diminutive bird gave us terrific, although brief, views. What a feeling to know that we were seeing a bird that is relatively new to science and limited in range. We ended the day looking for a Lesser Antillean Pewee at a nearby fishery, but were skunked. We would try again in the morning! Look for my Day 4 report in the next few days. I guarantee photos of boobies.</p><p><a href="http://www.hawkowlsnest.com/2010/02/puerto-rico-day-4-mountains-to-coast.html">Go to Day 4</a></p></p>
<div style='clear: both;'></div>

<h2 class='date-header'><span>Monday, February 01, 2010</span></h2>

        <div class="date-posts">
      
<div class='post-outer'>
<div class='post'>
<a name='5680341920453691782'></a>
<h3 class='post-title'>
<a href='http://www.hawkowlsnest.com/2010/02/puerto-rico-day-1-2.html'>Puerto Rico Day 1 & 2: Caribbean Gems</a>
</h3>
<div class='post-header-line-1'></div>
<div class='post-body'>
<p><div align="center"><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2eD77-uSfI/AAAAAAAABGE/oOvV-uXd1b8/s1600-h/Hotel+View.jpg"><img id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5433456541182085618" style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN: 0px auto 10px; WIDTH: 400px; CURSOR: hand; HEIGHT: 300px; TEXT-ALIGN: center" alt="" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2eD77-uSfI/AAAAAAAABGE/oOvV-uXd1b8/s400/Hotel+View.jpg" border="0" /></a> <em>The view from the hotel beach</em></div><div align="center"><br /></div><div align="center"><br /></div><div align="left">My friend Mike and I arrived the evening before our birding tour in Puerto Rico to avoid any potential weather-related events that might have caused flight issues. He and I toured around Old San Juan, ate some great local food thanks to a cab driver's recommendation, and drank VERY locally at a dive bar - $1.50 Medalla Light! Bird-wise, we only saw the ubiquitous <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bananaquit">Bananaquit</a> that first day.</div><div align="left"><br /></div><div align="left"></div><div align="left">We awoke the next morning and, as I opened the blinds of our balcony, a bird took off from the deck. A <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greater_Antillean_Grackle">Greater Antillean Grackle</a> had brought a chicken bone to our balcony and had been eating it there.</div><div align="center"><br /></div><div align="center"></div><img id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5433455999093625938" style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN: 0px auto 10px; WIDTH: 267px; CURSOR: hand; HEIGHT: 400px; TEXT-ALIGN: center" alt="" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2eDcYiw1FI/AAAAAAAABF0/EPT-40JGglo/s400/Grackle.jpg" border="0" /> <p align="center"><em>Greater Antillean Grackle</em></p><p align="left"><br />We birded around the hotel a bit where we saw more grackles, a Brown Pelican, <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red-legged_Thrush">Red-legged Thrush</a> (the Puerto Rican version of a robin), and <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zenaida_Dove">Zenaida Dove</a>.</p><br /><img id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5433456163136271794" style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN: 0px auto 10px; WIDTH: 400px; CURSOR: hand; HEIGHT: 266px; TEXT-ALIGN: center" alt="" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2eDl7pk9bI/AAAAAAAABF8/YuXa6zJM-N8/s400/zenaida+dove.jpg" border="0" /> <p align="center"><em>Zenaida Dove</em><br /></p><br /><br /><br />At 12:30, we met our leaders Kevin and Lena from <a href="http://www.wildsidetoursinc.com/">Wildside Nature Tours</a> and the two other tour participants. After a brief food and fuel stop, we headed west from San Juan toward the town of Hatillo. We made our first birding stop at Laguna Tortuguero, a small woodland area next to a large lake. We immediately started hearing and seeing some of our sought after <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_endemic_fauna_of_Puerto_Rico">Puerto Rican endemics</a>.<br /><br /><br />The first endemic we saw was <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adelaide">Adelaide's Warbler</a> - a gorgeous bird, but uncooperative for a photograph. Pearly-eyed Thrashers called from the undergrowth and several female <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Spindalis">Puerto Rican Spindalises</a> (Spindali?) flitted in the limbs of an <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orchid_tree">Orchid Tree</a>. Luck was with us and a splendid male Spindalis joined the party. He stayed just out of view for a while, but then came down ridiculously close to feed on the flower petals of the Orchid Tree.<br /><br /><br /><br /><img id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5433456994345938882" style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN: 0px auto 10px; WIDTH: 400px; CURSOR: hand; HEIGHT: 267px; TEXT-ALIGN: center" alt="" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2eEWUJZ78I/AAAAAAAABGM/qzZ8V4QFtF8/s400/Spindalis01.jpg" border="0" /> <p align="center"><em>PR Spindalis with a piece of petal in his mouth</em><br /></p><p align="left"><br />A hummingbird made itself known by buzzing over the canopy of the tree. It was a female <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antillean_Mango">Antillean Mango</a> - a specialty of the Caribbean.</p><br /><img id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5433457101981335666" style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN: 0px auto 10px; WIDTH: 267px; CURSOR: hand; HEIGHT: 400px; TEXT-ALIGN: center" alt="" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_2gstGUqAi0c/S2eEclHrwHI/AAAAAAAABGU/rA9zmso3m1g/s400/Antillean+Mango+Female.jpg" border="0" /> <p align="center"><em>Antillean Mango - the leaf is not really stuck to the end of his bill, just bad positioning in the photo<br /></em><br /></p><p><br /><br />We also saw some familiar birds like Osprey and Northern Parula and less familiar ones like the introduced <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orange_cheeked_waxbill">Orange-cheeked Waxbill</a>. We ended our time there and continued to our hotel for the night. I had a great dinner of some eggplant dish with a delicious side of rice and beans, along with some flan de vanilla for dessert. Yum. We were off to a terrific start! Day 3 was filled with tremendous birds. More on that later. </p><p><a href="http://www.hawkowlsnest.com/2010/02/puerto-rico-day-3-rare-birds-and.html">Go to day 3</a></p></p>
<div style='clear: both;'></div>

<h2 class='date-header'><span>Monday, January 25, 2010</span></h2>

        <div class="date-posts">
      
<div class='post-outer'>
<div class='post'>
<a name='6827955461069781906'></a>
<h3 class='post-title'>
<a href='http://www.hawkowlsnest.com/2010/01/off-to-puerto-rico.html'>Off to Puerto Rico</a>
</h3>
<div class='post-header-line-1'></div>
<div class='post-body'>
<p>For those who didn't see it on Twitter or Facebook... I'll be leaving for Puerto Rico tomorrow for <a href="http://www.wildsidetoursinc.com/itineraries/puerto_rico_dash.html">5 days of birding adventure</a>. The actual tour doesn't start until mid-day on Wednesday. Where connectivity is available, I will be tweeting and blogging about the trip. It should be a blast. Thanks again to the guys from <a href="http://www.10000birds.com/">10,000 Birds</a> for sponsoring the contest. Endemics, quite a few exotics, and neat West Indian birds await!</p>
<div style='clear: both;'></div>
</div>

<h2>Other Sites</h2>

  function GetDay(intDay){
    var DayArray = new Array("Sunday", "Monday", "Tuesday", "Wednesday", 
                         "Thursday", "Friday", "Saturday")
    return DayArray[intDay]
    }

  function GetMonth(intMonth){
    var MonthArray = new Array("January", "February", "March",
                               "April", "May", "June",
                               "July", "August", "September",
                               "October", "November", "December") 
    return MonthArray[intMonth] 	  	 
    }
  function getDateStrWithDOW(){
    var today = new Date()
    var year = today.getYear()
    if(year<1000) year+=1900
    var todayStr = GetDay(today.getDay()) + ", "
    todayStr += GetMonth(today.getMonth()) + " " + today.getDate()
    todayStr += ", " + year
    return todayStr
    }

+OpenLayer+"<a href='http://www.bbc.co.uk/weather/coast/tides/wales.shtml' target='_bank')' class='x'>Tides</a>"+CloseLayer
+OpenLayer+"<a href='http://www.bbc.co.uk/weather/coast/shipping/' target='_bank')' class='x'>Shipping Forecast</a>"+CloseLayer

//!!!Alter anything past this point!!!

w1=(MenuWidth+Separater)*Titles.length;
w2=w/2;
i1=w2-MenuWidth-Separater-w1/2;
i2=w2-MenuWidth-Separater-w1/2;
s1=MenuWidth+Separater;
s2=MenuWidth+Separater;
if (w1 > w2*2){i1=-MenuWidth;i2=-MenuWidth}
vy=(n4)?'show':'visible';
vn=(n4)?'hide':'hidden';

//Don't mess about with N4, just use layers.
if (n4){
for (i=0; i < Titles.length; i++){
document.write("<layer name='lnks"+i+"' top=0 left="+(i2+=s2)+" "
+" width="+MenuWidth+" bgcolor="+HighLight+" visibility=hide"
+" onMouseOver='this.visibility=vy; var cd=this.id.length-1; var ab=this.id.charAt(cd); H(ab)' "
+" onMouseOut='this.visibility=vn; var ef=this.id.length-1; var gh=this.id.charAt(ef); B(gh)'>"
+algn1+"<font face="+MenuFont+" size="+MenuFontSize+">"
+"&nbsp;<br>"+Links[i]+"</font>"+algn2+"</layer>");
document.write("<layer name='ttls"+i+"' top=0 left="+(i1+=s1)+" height=0 " 
+"width="+MenuWidth+" bgcolor="+MenuBgColor+" "
+"onMouseOver=\"this.bgColor=HighLight; var e=this.id.length-1; var d=this.id.charAt(e); On(d)\" "
+"onMouseOut=\"this.bgColor=MenuBgColor; var e=this.id.length-1; var d=this.id.charAt(e); Off(d)\">"
+algn1+"<font face="+MenuFont+" size="+MenuFontSize+" color="+MenuFontColor+">"
+Titles[i]+"</font>"+algn2+"</layer>");                                       
}
function On(x){for (i=0; i < Titles.length; i++)document.layers['lnks'+x].visibility=vy}
function Off(x){for (i=0; i < Titles.length; i++)document.layers['lnks'+x].visibility=vn}
function B(y){for (i=0; i < Titles.length; i++)document.layers['ttls'+y].bgColor=MenuBgColor}
function H(y){for (i=0; i < Titles.length; i++)document.layers['ttls'+y].bgColor=HighLight}
}
if (!n4){
for (i=0; i < Titles.length; i++){
document.write("<div id='lnks"+i+"' style='position:absolute;"
+"top:0px;left:"+(i2+=s2)+"px;width:"+MenuWidth+"px;"
+"background:"+HighLight+";visibility:hidden'" 
+" onMouseOver='this.style.visibility=vy; document.getElementById(\"ttls"+i+"\").style.background=HighLight';"
+" onMouseOut='this.style.visibility=vn; document.getElementById(\"ttls"+i+"\").style.background=MenuBgColor'>"
+algn1+Links[i]+algn2+"</div>");
document.write("<div id='ttls"+i+"' style='position:absolute;top:0px;left:"+(i1+=s1)+"px;height:auto;width:"+MenuWidth+"px;"
+"background:"+MenuBgColor+";cursor:default'"
+" onMouseOver='document.getElementById(\"lnks"+i+"\").style.visibility=vy;this.style.background=HighLight'" 
+" onMouseOut='document.getElementById(\"lnks"+i+"\").style.visibility=vn;this.style.background=MenuBgColor'>"
+algn1+"<font face="+MenuFont+" size="+MenuFontSize+" color="+MenuFontColor+">"+Titles[i]+"</font>"+algn2+"</div>");
}
}
function Scroll(){
sy=(ie)?document.body.scrollTop:window.pageYOffset;
for (i=0; i < Titles.length; i++){
if (n4){
 document.layers['ttls'+i].top=Separater+sy;
 document.layers['lnks'+i].top=Separater+sy;
 }
else{
 document.getElementById("ttls"+i).style.top=Separater+sy;
 document.getElementById("lnks"+i).style.top=Separater+sy;
 }
}
setTimeout('Scroll()',150)
}
Scroll();
window.onresize=new Function("window.location.reload()");


if (!n4){
for (i=0; i < document.links.length; i++){
 if (document.links[i].href == this.window.location.href)
  {
  document.links[i].style.color=MenuBgColor;
  document.links[i].style.cursor='crosshair';
  //document.links[i].innerHTML+=' -';
  //alert(i+' '+document.links[i].href);
  break;
  }
 }
}
